The grades were divided using the words "Min Gen Gong Cong Yan Wu," with 290 "Min" relief tickets, 2,071 "Gen" tickets, 2,187 "Gong" tickets, 563 "Cong" tickets, and 268 "Yan" tickets, for a total of 5,379 relief tickets. They were divided into five grades, with "Min" tickets worth two dou of relief rice, "Gen" tickets worth two and a half dou, "Gong" tickets worth three dou, "Cong" tickets worth four and a half dou, and "Yan" tickets worth five dou, for a total of 1,619 shi and two dou of relief rice. Relief clothing consisted of one jacket and one pair of trousers using the words "Jia Hui," for a total of 704 sets plus one piece of relief clothing. In addition, 160 shi of relief rice was reissued to returning refugees and impoverished people. In total, 18,223 relief tickets were surveyed and issued in Districts 4, 5, 6, and 3, totaling 31,100 yuan of relief and 1,604 sets plus one piece of relief clothing. A total of 1,779 shi and two dou of relief rice were issued. When surveying and distributing in each district, the legal associations of the county were invited to send representatives to supervise the distribution. The actual distribution was completed on January 31. With so many disaster victims and so little relief, who with a heart can not feel endless regret?

Attorney He Sui Accused of Embezzlement 182

Attorney He Sui was recently prosecuted by Mao Tianshui of Ningbo in the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court for embezzlement and requested to be investigated according to law. The court, based on the complaint, summoned him yesterday by Judge Li Changnian in Criminal Court 2. First, the plaintiff Mao Tianshui stated that he was a merchant who opened the Mao Maotai Wood Shop at No. 1595 Jing'an Temple Road. Due to market influences, he was short of funds and had to close the business. He was introduced by his friend Chen Bingkun to hire attorney He Sui to represent him in the liquidation. At that time, the official fee was 100 yuan and the clerk fee was 15 yuan. Later, he sold the shop base to Mao Shangxian for business, priced at 1,400 yuan. The debts were shared equally, but only one creditor, Chen Shuchang, totaling 413 yuan, did not agree to a discount. Therefore, the merchant had no choice but to raise funds from relatives and friends. Mao Shangxian issued a check for 413 yuan from the China Reclamation Bank and handed it to attorney He to entrust him to transfer it to creditor Chen Shuchang for receipt. Unexpectedly, He did not transfer the money, so creditor Chen Shuchang filed a lawsuit against the merchant in court. When I questioned He, he claimed that the money had been used for official fees. In this situation, attorney He clearly committed the crime of embezzlement. Please investigate and deal with it according to law. Then, witness Chen Bingkun stated that when the plaintiff's shop closed and was liquidated, I introduced him to attorney He. I was also present when the plaintiff handed over the money to He and saw a check being handed over. Mao Shangxian stated that the check returned by the plaintiff to Chen Shuchang was actually issued by the merchant. The first time, the name of the check was Chen Shuchang, the holder. Attorney He stamped it and went to the bank to collect the money, but it was returned because the name did not match. So he exchanged it with me again. The name on the check was Attorney He Sui. There is a first returned check as proof. Please examine it. When asked, the defendant He Sui did not arrive. A lawyer arrived on his behalf, claiming that He went to the local court to appear in court, so he did not arrive. He requested a postponement. The official said that the defendant submitted a statement of defense and a counterclaim for slander. After issuing a copy to the plaintiff, he ordered a postponement for further questioning.

Check Case of Pirated Robbery Transferred to Local Court 183

Between December 6th of last year, the Xinhai Gate Steamboat was robbed by pirates on the high seas, and passengers were kidnapped and held for ransom. At that time, a passenger from Taizhou named Wang Wanhe received a Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation check for 100 yuan with number 238966 from a woman. Wang came to Shanghai and went to Wang Xingji, a fellow villager who ran a carpentry business on Qingyun Road in Zhabei, asking him to go to the branch on Broadway to cash it. (It was discovered that the check was lost by an employee of the Anglican Church Council under the jurisdiction of Ningbo Yin County, Zhejiang Province, and a telegram had been sent to cancel it). The bank telegraphed the Hongkou Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Detective Huang Guangqi to secretly arrest the two Wangs and send them to the First Special District Court. After several interrogations, Wang Wanhe was ordered to be detained, and Wang Xingji was released on bail, as previously reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Zehan continued the trial in the Third Criminal Court. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, recounted the previous events. However, the Yin County Procuratorate sent a letter stating that it would not transfer the case, and the person who lost the check never appeared in court to testify. Wang Xingji, who was released on bail, did not appear. Lawyer Li stated that the case occurred on the sea, within the jurisdiction of Yin County, and since the case was not being transferred, it should be sent to the inland authorities. Judge Wu ordered that the case be transferred to the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate for review. Wang Wanhe was allowed to be transferred to the Civil Detention Center, and Wang Xingji was notified to surrender himself to the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate.

Zeng Pu's Famous Work "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" Third Edition Published 184

The book "A Flower in a Sinful Sea" is the most proud work of the "Sick Man of East Asia" (i.e., Mr. Zeng Pu). It has long been a household name. I believe we can all recall the author's lengthy conversation a month ago, explaining the origins of the protagonist Sai Jinhua's story, which was published in the newspapers. Ms. Sai was indeed a famous figure during the庚子 year. She often rode in and out of the palace with General Waldersee, the leader of the Allied Forces, with officials bowing their heads. Now, she is old and frail, living in the old capital. The glory of the past is like a dream. Readers who savor this book cannot help but feel emotional. The book also narrates many anecdotes and interesting stories from the Qing Dynasty, full of humor. The delicacy of the writing and the transcendence of the style are particularly noteworthy. The original manuscript of the book has sold more than ten editions, totaling over 200,000 copies, which is already unprecedented. Later, Zeng Pu revised the entire book, making it even more exciting. Now, a third edition of the revised book has been published. The entire book is divided into three parts, forming a large, thick volume, beautifully bound in Western style. The actual selling price is only one dollar and twenty cents. The general distributor is the editorial department of the Shanghai Great Evening News, and all major bookstores in various regions are selling it.

The International Grand Hotel has only been open for a little over two months, but its business is booming. This is due to its reasonable prices and attentive service. Its magnificent decorations are truly captivating, and its exquisite cuisine is even more tempting. Now that it is the beginning of the lunar year, various circles traditionally hold spring banquets, and this custom cannot be avoided. The hotel, as a leader among upscale hotels, caters to this demand, and people have been rushing to make reservations in recent days. The hotel, in order to provide attentive service, has specially assigned staff to manage the event, and they are overwhelmed with requests.

Laiyang Pear Paste is Indeed a Holy Medicine for Curing Coughs 188

The Yuanshou brand Laiyang pear paste, produced by the Yantai Dongya Company and distributed by the Yicheng Company on Tongfu Road in Shanghai, is a holy medicine for curing coughs. It has been sold in various ports and has long been famous. Among the best pear varieties, Laiyang pears from Shandong Province are the top choice, with a delicate texture and a sweet and honey-like taste. When made into pear paste with川貝母 (Chuan Bei Mu), it is truly different from ordinary pear paste sold on the market. It functions to resolve phlegm, relieve coughs, moisten the lungs, and reduce internal heat. Now that it is the cold spring season and the weather is dry, those suffering from coughs will surely see immediate results if they take Laiyang pear paste regularly.

Paramount's New Year's Banquet and Dance 189

"Encyclopedia of English Calligraphy" Published Mr. Liang Huiran, former representative of Popular University of America in China and Master of Fine Arts and Calligraphy, has a deep understanding of English calligraphy. Recently, seeing that there are many people in our country learning English, but little attention is paid to the study of English calligraphy, he wrote the "Encyclopedia of English Calligraphy" based on his usual teaching experience to guide future students. The book has rich content, novel compilation methods, and covers commercial signature methods, fine art business cards, calligraphy, English portrait calligraphy, and flowers, birds, and animal gardens, etc., categorized and inclusive, allowing calligraphy learners to simultaneously obtain various practical commercial knowledge. It is truly a masterpiece. The book also contains the calligraphy of the names of great people at home and abroad, which is even more valuable. Dr. Wei Ke, former Director of the Shanghai Special City Education Bureau, said that the book has novel materials and is extremely practical. Students in large, medium, and small schools can all use it as a reference and self-study model. The entire book has recently been published, and those who are interested in studying English calligraphy should each purchase a copy to use as a model.

Letters to the Editor 197

To the Editor: We read in the news column of your newspaper on February 8th that the City Government will inspect the smallpox vaccine sold in the city, which stated, "It has been found that the four brands of smallpox vaccine sold in Hankou, namely Qilin, Triangle, Zhongxi, and Fushou, have been tested and found to be ineffective." We would like to clarify that the Zhongxi brand mentioned is not the smallpox vaccine brand produced by our company. It is obviously a counterfeit. The product produced by our company is the "Nine Star Brand Smallpox Vaccine." The one sold by the Hankou branch is also the Nine Star brand. We are deeply afraid that the outside world will not know the truth and will easily misunderstand. We hereby solemnly request you to correct it. Sincerely, Promotion Department, Zhongxi Pharmaceutical Co., Ltd., February 8, 24th Year.

To the Editor: We read in your newspaper's news column of this city on the 8th of this month, "News from various fellow villagers associations," "Carrying a news of a meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee to thoroughly investigate member Wang Chengbao and others' accusation of the Director of the First Section," which is untrue. Recently, our association discovered a leaflet distributed to members. The content of the leaflet, bearing the name of Wang Chengbao, is that of a deceased member. It is obviously fabricated slander, of the same nature as an anonymous posting. Moreover, the joint meeting of our Executive Supervisory Committee was held at 2:00 p.m. on the 7th of this month to discuss the leaflet incident. It was unanimously agreed that "Director Zhang's morality and reputation are trusted by the society. Since taking office as the Director of our Association, he has achieved excellent results, which are admired by fellow villagers. This kind of unintentional action is not enough to damage Director Zhang's reputation. Moreover, what it refers to has no value whatsoever. It should be ignored. Please Director Zhang do not mind," etc., recorded in the minutes. There was no meeting scheduled for 3:00 p.m. on February 10th. We request your newspaper to correct it to show the truth. We hereby inform you and hope that you will handle it accordingly. Sincerely, Standing Committee of Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, February 8th.

Dear Editor: I have read the column about the improvement of the porcelain industry in Jiangxi Province on page 15 of the fourth sheet of your newspaper on the 7th of this month. It said that a reporter from the National Society visited me and said that the Jiangxi Provincial Government decided to establish a large-scale porcelain company called the Guangda Porcelain Company in order to improve the porcelain in Jiangxi Province, with a registered capital of 7 million yuan, jointly operated by the government and merchants, with the government holding 2 million yuan, determined by the Jiangxi Provincial Government, and the merchants holding 5 million yuan, which will be raised in Shanghai and is expected to be raised within March, etc. It is true that I am in charge of the Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Company, but the registered capital is 1 million yuan, with the Jiangxi Provincial Government contributing 200,000 yuan, and the rest will be raised by me, not limited to Shanghai. I have only published a message once in the New Life Weekly that I run, and have not spoken to any reporters. I do not even know what the National Society is. This news is obviously based on hearsay and is untrue. I request you to correct it. In this country with a backward industry, there is no new production news that can be published. The reporter from the National Society may have used this small porcelain company to exaggerate the story and arouse the attention of the people. The intention may be good, but all the news is said to be from my mouth, which is related to personal credibility. Moreover, I have always advocated pragmatism. Such a false show of strength is also tasteless. I hereby request the editor of your newspaper to quickly correct it. Sincerely, Du Chongyuan, February 7th evening.

To the Editor: In the news item in your newspaper on the 8th of this month, "Notice from the Tobacco and Salt Industry to Fellow Businesses to Distribute Inspection Scales," it was stated, "Kerosene scales, now manufactured by the City Inspection Bureau (divided into two, four, and eight taels, each set for six corners), will be distributed immediately, and all businesses must collect them for inspection." We would like to clarify that our office has never manufactured or distributed any weights and measures, nor has the Industry Association sent the scales to our office for inspection, nor has our office conducted inspections. Moreover, the legal unit of measurement for liquid measuring instruments is liters, 合 (ge), and 勺 (shao), which is inconsistent with the Association's use of斤 (jin) and 兩 (liang). Please publish this letter to correct it. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Weights and Measures Inspection, February 8th.

To the Esteemed Chief Editor of Shen Bao: We, the Qian Tai shop, are writing to you. In the local news column of your newspaper on the 7th of this month, a news article was published titled "Lawsuit for Imitating Star Brand Coffee and Tea Trademark," which stated that Qian Tai Confectionery Company intentionally sold counterfeit Star Brand coffee and tea, etc., which is inconsistent with the facts. Our shop has been open for many years and has never committed any illegal acts. The counterfeit Star Brand coffee and tea were brought by a partner from a closed company in Guangzhou to peddle. On that day, the shop's accountant was busy entertaining guests because his child was one month old, so he mistakenly recognized it as a product of the Guangzhou company and accepted it due to oversight. Although a fine was imposed, we are not willing to accept it and are now appealing according to law. It concerns the reputation of our shop, so we are writing this respectful letter to request you to truthfully correct it to reflect the facts. We look forward to your assistance and wish you good health. Sincerely, Qian Tai Shop, north end of the vegetable market in the French Concession, February 8th.

Weather Report 198

Xujiahui Observatory predicted at 4:30 PM yesterday that the weather around Shandong is cloudy and cold, but still fine, with undefined wind direction; the middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and cold, with intermittent rain or snow, and the wind comes from the northeast to northwest, due to a small low pressure passing and moving eastward; there is rain in the East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait, and the wind is from the northeast to southeast. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 46.8 and the lowest was 32.7. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 47.8 and the lowest was 25.9.

Tense Situation: Black Eagles Lose to Donghua 207

44 to 52, a difference of 8 points

Fouls Accumulate, Three Players Ejected

The Qingdao Black Eagles basketball team made their second appearance at the Shen Garden Basketball Hall last night, but unfortunately lost to Donghua. The final score was 52 to 44, a difference of only 8 points. The Black Eagles took the lead in the first half, but Donghua intensified their efforts in the second half, gradually catching up. The score fluctuated, sometimes with a difference of only two or three points. The tension of the situation was unparalleled.

Kong Guangyi's Long Shots Amaze 208

The most exciting part of the first half was Kong Guangyi's long shots. Almost nine out of ten shots went in, leaving the Donghua players with nothing but helpless sighs. Initially, the Black Eagles were behind 10 to 11, trailing by one point. Kong Guangyi made three long shots, bringing the score to 16 to 12, taking the lead. Sun Baoqing charged out from under the basket, and Donghua chased the score to 16 to 18. Then, Ding Shouyu, a key player for the Black Eagles, was ejected for four fouls. However, the Black Eagles still maintained their lead. At halftime, the Black Eagles were ahead by three points, 25 to 22.

Donghua Team Catches Up 209

From the start of the second half, Donghua showed a sudden surge in energy, breaking through and charging, with excellent coordination among the three forwards. As expected, they scored three consecutive baskets, tying the score at 28 each. Then, Xiang Long scored, immediately pushing the score to 30 to 28, giving Donghua the lead over the Black Eagles. Subsequently, the score became 33 each, and then 37 to 36, with Donghua ahead by one point. Xiang Long was then ejected for four fouls. The Black Eagles did manage to tie the score at 41. However, Feng Nianhua scored four points consecutively, and Kong Guangyi, the main player, was also fouled out. The Black Eagles were ultimately unable to recover, and the final score was 52 to 44, with Donghua winning.

(Dentsu, Tokyo, 8th) It has been decided that Japan will send athletes to the International Olympics to be held in Berlin next year on August 8th and the Winter Olympics to be held in Garmisch-Partenkirchen next year in February. Yan Jici Elected as Director of the French Physical Society 218

The French Physical Society has been established for more than sixty years and has more than 1,300 members, all of whom are contemporary physicists. In addition to officers such as the president, vice president, secretary, and accountant, its organization includes a board of directors, which plans all the proceedings of the society. The board of directors has a total of 24 directors, with one-third being re-elected each year. Among the eight newly elected directors this year, two are non-French citizens: one is Professor Kapltza of Cambridge University in England, and the other is Dr. Yan Jici, director of the Institute of Physics of the Peiping Research Institute. Among the old directors who have completed their terms and are leaving this year, there are also two non-French citizens: one is Professor Gerlach of the University of Munich in Germany, and the other is Professor Lyman of Harvard University in the United States. It is said that there is still one Asian in the current board of directors, namely Professor Raman, an Indian physicist who won the Nobel Prize in 1930.

Jiangsu Luhe Slaughter Tax Bidding 219

Jiang Yiming, the director in charge of collecting slaughter tax in Luhe County, Jiangsu, owed too much tax and has been removed from his position. Bidding is being re-invited, with the base amount reduced to 5,200 yuan. The bidding is scheduled to take place on February 20th at the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office on Tinghou Street in Nanjing. Bidders must pay a deposit of one-twentieth of the amount, about 260 yuan. If the bid is successful, it will be deducted from the deposit. If the bid is unsuccessful, the original amount will be refunded.

Municipal Education Association Continues to Operate a People's School 223

School Address: Jumen Road, Nanshi

All Expenses are Waived

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association attaches great importance to popular education. In order to concentrate efforts and save funds, the Board of Directors has decided to continue operating the First People's School and to establish it as a permanent institution. The Executive Director Huang Zaoxiong has been appointed as the principal. The school is located at Zhangjiabang, Jumen Road, Nanshi. The enrollment is tentatively set at 50 students. Registration will take place from the 25th to the 28th of this month, and classes will begin on March 1st. Uneducated men and women between the ages of 16 and 50 can register and enroll in the school. Students currently studying at other schools will not be admitted. Tuition is free, and books and stationery are provided by the school. However, students must find a guarantor to fill out a guarantee form and pay a deposit of one yuan at the time of enrollment, which will be refunded upon graduation as a form of restriction. Students who are expelled for violating regulations or withdraw from school for no reason will have their deposits confiscated. The graduation period is set at four months, with two hours of classes per day, tentatively scheduled from 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM. In addition, the association has launched a weekly publication called "Citizen Life" to train the general public in civic knowledge. It is divided into sections such as commentary, common sense, literature and art, and current affairs news, targeting workers and shop apprentices as readers. The first issue is scheduled to be published on the 16th of this month.

National Mandarin Education Promotion Association Holds Mandarin Lectures on Radio Stations 224

In order to promote Mandarin education, the National Mandarin Education Promotion Association has designated this year as the Mandarin Construction Year and decided to do one type of work each month. In February, it launched the National Radio Station Mandarin Lecture Series, with education directors and Mandarin experts from various places giving lectures on local radio stations. Except for Sundays, there will be lectures every day. On February 1st, the Minister of Education gave a lecture at the Central Radio Station in Nanjing, stating that "Writing is the foundation of national revival, but Chinese writing is difficult, not easy to learn, and inconvenient to use. Therefore, this Ministry has promulgated phonetic symbols and Mandarin Romanization to help literacy. Phonetic symbols and Mandarin Romanization should be learned and used not only by students at all levels and the general public, but also by intellectuals, so that they can be closer to everyone and revive the nation." On the 2nd, Cai Yuanpei, the president of the association, gave a lecture at the Shanghai Broadcasting Station, advocating for "(1) Primary school textbooks should not use classical Chinese, but Mandarin. (2) Textbooks for popular education should all use Mandarin. (3) Phonetic symbols should be added next to the Mandarin characters. The initial textbooks should use phonetic symbols only, without referring to old characters. (4) Teachers must have received Mandarin training." Yesterday, Zhao Yuanren, a director of the association, gave a lecture at the Central Radio Station in Nanjing, stating that the living intonation can be divided into three types: tone, central intonation, and expressive intonation.

Report of the National Labor Exhibition General Review (3) 228

(C) Civil Engineering Department Achievement

The various subjects within the scope of civil engineering, such as river and sea engineering, sanitary engineering, and road and bridge engineering, have student achievements that are inconvenient to transport and cannot be compared with other ordinary works, where the completion of one piece can be submitted to the exhibition as an achievement. Therefore, the number of civil engineering exhibits at this exhibition is far less than that of other parts. Among the civil engineering achievements submitted by various provinces and cities, the library design drawings of the Civil Engineering Department of Shanghai Jingye Middle School, the Danyang Lianhu Lake Consolidation Plan (model) of Danyang Private Zhengze Elementary School in Jiangsu Province, the surveying and material testing reports of the Civil Engineering Department of Zhejiang Advanced Industrial Vocational School, the wooden bridge model and several measured maps of the vicinity of Anhui Province of Anhui Provincial First Secondary Vocational School, the steel model of the Civil Engineering Department of the High School Engineering Department of Hunan Private Chuyi Middle School, the projection geometric model and bridge, roof truss, culvert and other models of the Advanced Civil Engineering Department of Fujian Provincial Fuzhou Industrial Vocational School, etc., can all reflect the school's spirit and organization of teaching, as well as the students' usual experiments and design. They are quite commendable, but among these exhibits, there are more models and fewer design drawings and planning reports, which is not without its shortcomings. Because the achievements of civil engineering students that can be displayed at exhibitions actually belong to the latter two items, while models are a tool to aid teaching, not formal achievements of civil engineering students. This is quite different from the labor work of primary and secondary schools. During the next exhibition, schools should be instructed to pay attention to this.

(D) Dyeing and Weaving Department 229

The dyeing and weaving department was originally one of the industrial education specialties. In China's commercial ports, the dyeing and weaving industry is oppressed by the import of foreign goods, and most of the manual occupations of this industry have almost no possibility of existence. Therefore, the vocational education facilities and teaching of this department are particularly difficult. At this exhibition, there were not many dyeing and weaving exhibits. Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, which are known as the most developed dyeing and weaving areas, had very few exhibits. The three provinces of Shandong, Henan, and Hunan had richer exhibits, with remarkable achievements. The ability of Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Chahar provinces to utilize local raw materials for research and manufacturing is particularly commendable. The carpets in the orphanages of Xi'an are especially unique. The northwestern provinces have abundant raw materials and lower wages. This type of manual dyeing and weaving industry is very necessary to promote and has great prospects for development.

(E) Applied Chemistry Subject Results 230

1. General Assessment

In this exhibition, the applied chemistry exhibits were roughly divided into pottery, glass, printing, leather making, soap, paint, cosmetics, stationery, porcelain, paper, and other items. The exhibiting schools included 31 vocational schools and 7 middle schools (due to the special nature of Xiangshan Orphanage, it is classified as a vocational school). Many exhibits are locally sourced and cater to local needs. However, some exhibits are blindly copied or are impractical conglomerations. To improve the efficiency of vocational education, schools should focus on specialized training to achieve excellence in the future.

2. Specific Assessments

A. Special Exhibits Category: Includes items of a unique nature or those with too few entries for meaningful comparison.

(1) The glass from the Jiangsu Provincial Suqian Vocational School's Glass Department and the pottery from the Jiangsu Yixing Ceramics Vocational School both utilize local materials and have achieved excellent results.

(2) Although the exhibits from the Hubei Provincial Vocational School's Printing Department are of a general applied chemical industrial nature, since no other schools submitted printing exhibits, they are included in this category for comparison. The results are also considered excellent.

(3) The porcelain from Jiangxi and the lacquerware from Fujian (both chemical industries) were assessed.

Although these were not initially included in the applied chemistry category, given their long-standing reputation, they are specially highlighted.

B. Comparable Exhibits Category: Includes items with a sufficient number of entries for comparison.

(1) Leather Making: Leather making had the most applied chemistry exhibits, with over 20 exhibiting schools, demonstrating the position of the leather industry in vocational education and the promising future of the leather industry. Many schools have achieved noteworthy results, with the leather making departments of the Hebei Provincial Institute of Technology Affiliated Vocational Department, the Beiping Advanced Vocational School, and the Suzhou Middle School Chemistry Department being particularly outstanding, especially the Institute of Technology's Affiliated Vocational Department.

(2) Soap: Soap making is relatively easy to practice, so many schools submitted exhibits. Among the perfumed soaps, those from the Hebei Provincial Baoding Advanced Vocational School were the best. Among the bar soaps, those from the Suzhou Middle School Chemistry Department were the best.

(3) Paint: Seven schools submitted paint exhibits, with those from the Hubei Provincial Vocational School being relatively superior.

(4) Cosmetics: In cosmetics manufacturing, the raw materials and blending methods are crucial, and external packaging is also highly relevant. Among the exhibits, those from the Hunan Provincial Vocational School were the best. Schools researching cosmetics should focus on the manufacturing of raw materials and the blending of solvents. Simply purchasing ready-made raw materials, solvents, and packaging and then blending them is a waste of time and effort and is not economical. This is specifically mentioned for reference.

(5) Stationery: Stationery includes ink, printing ink, chalk, paste, stencil paper, etc. While there were many excellent exhibits, they are less important from an applied chemistry perspective.

(6) Porcelain and Paper: Porcelain and paper are both unique inventions of our country, and the paper industry is particularly significant for culture. The number of exhibits in this exhibition was small compared to other applied chemistry categories, and there were no outstanding results, except for the porcelain from Jiangxi. This is specially mentioned to draw attention to the vocational education sector.

(F) Business Subject Results 231

The number of commercial schools exhibiting at this labor exhibition was extremely small. Regrettably, the results from Shanghai, which is recognized nationwide as a commercial center, were lower than those of other provinces and cities. The areas from commercial schools that we can observe include accounting, statistics, typing, and advertising. Reports generated from accounting books can show the income, expenses, and financial condition of agricultural, industrial, and commercial enterprises. Charts and graphs created based on statistical methods can show the production and sales situation of agricultural, industrial, and commercial enterprises, and their economic position among domestic counterparts. Typing and advertising are auxiliary tools for promoting agricultural and industrial products, and are unique subjects for commercial schools. Although the submissions from various provinces and cities touched on accounting, typing, statistics, and advertising, only a few achieved excellent results. Accounting is a particularly important subject, but there was no presentation of good results. The poor results from commercial schools is an undeniable fact. There were more statistical charts and graphs with good results, excluding those from the Zhejiang Education Department, Fujian Education Department, and Qingdao Municipal Government, which were not subject to criticism. The comparative charts produced by the Hangzhou Women's Commercial School, the agricultural product index charts produced by the Shanxi Mingxian School, the comparative charts produced by the Beiping Municipal Advanced Commercial School, and the price index table produced by the Anhui Provincial First Vocational School were all well-organized and worthy of study. This labor exhibition included various light industries such as agricultural products, textiles, embroidery, pottery, and woodwork, lacquerware, and heavy industries such as machinery, in significant numbers. However, the cost and output statistics of the products and the comparisons over the years were not specified, which is a shortcoming. Only the Shanxi Mingxian School provided detailed statistics on the output and soil distribution of agricultural products over the years, using indices and charts, which is highly commendable.

News from Various Schools 232

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Commercial Night School: The number of students at the commercial night school established by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce increased to 1,400 last semester. Enrollment for the current semester has begun. Li Quanshi, Yang Yinpu, Yao Qingsan, Li Wenjie, and others have been newly hired as professors. The specialized course level is equivalent to a university specialty and follows the Ministry of Education's regulations, requiring 72 credits for graduation. It is currently divided into banking and accounting departments. In addition, a specialized accounting course is co-organized with accountant Xu Yongzuo, divided into elementary and advanced classes, each graduating in two semesters. High school and school graduates can enroll without examination. Tuition is 20 yuan per semester for the elementary accounting specialty and 25 yuan for all others. The general course is divided into ten classes, with sessions in the early and late groups. The early group is from 6:45 PM to 8:15 PM, and the late group is from 8:30 PM to 10:00 PM. Graduates of the general course are equivalent to senior high school. Tuition for the first to fifth classes is 11 yuan for the early group and 9 yuan for the late group, and for the sixth to tenth classes, it is 13 yuan for the early group and 11 yuan for the late group. In addition to the specialized courses, the elective courses include: (1) Chinese language class (3 semesters), (2) Japanese language class (2 semesters), (3) Bookkeeping class, (4) Improved Chinese bookkeeping class, (5) Mathematics class, divided into geometry and algebra groups, (6) Chinese typing class (graduating in three months per term), and (7) Correspondence class, designed for those who cannot attend school regularly due to their work.

Minguo Girls' Middle School: Since being approved for establishment, the school affairs of Minguo Girls' Middle School on Weihaiwei Road and Chengdu Road have progressed daily. This semester, due to the large number of students, there are plans to establish two departments to expand the school. To select talent and focus on teaching, the school has published advertisements to recruit teachers, showing its seriousness. The school opened yesterday, but there are still vacancies in various grades.

Hudong Commercial Vocational Middle School: Hudong Commercial Vocational Middle School on Baker Road has specially established a public scribe service and a common knowledge guidance center, providing free services. It also allows residents near the Ant and Shenbao libraries to read and inquire during their spare time, which has been very beneficial. The founder of the school, Mr. Chen, has set up 40 free places for the children of poor workers in the Eastern District.

Several Points to Study Regarding Short Wavelengths 233

— Jian

The importance of studying short wavelengths is something that all of us in the wireless radio industry can talk about. However, what should be studied? Here are a few important points, and I hope to discuss them together with amateur researchers.

I. Regarding Transmitters:

(1) Stability of oscillation frequency.

(2) Use of high power.

(3) Shape of the transmitting antenna (including directional antennas).

II. Regarding Radios:

(1) Receiving method.

(2) Review of tuning.

III. Regarding Transmission Distance:

(1) Relationship between short wavelength and transmission distance.

(2) Relationship between power and transmission distance.

(3) Relationship between direction and transmission distance.

IV. Regarding Radio Wave Propagation:

(1) Theories of radio wave propagation.

(2) Experiments on radio wave propagation.

The Most Economical Shortwave Transmitter 234

— Chen Xianwen

Manufacturing and Economics that Best Suit Amateurs

Recently, I often see many styles of transmitters in magazines. At the time, I felt itchy in my heart. Although I wanted to try it, I was disappointed due to economic constraints. Recently, I tried a most economical method, costing only a few tens of dollars, which can create a transmitter with an output capacity of more than 5 watts.

The oscillation part of this machine is not much different from what is usually seen. The only difference is the power supply part; and the most economical is also this part. Ordinary power transformers must be purchased ready-made, or they must be made by yourself. But buying ready-made goods is expensive and does not fit the tastes of amateurs. Then you have to make it yourself, but the difficulty is winding the wire; because the transmitter requires a very high screen voltage, if you want to wind a half-wave rectified high-voltage coil, you need two or three thousand turns, and most of the ordinary ones (ie small transformers) use about No. 30 or so thinner wires, so it is even more difficult to wind. If you add a primary coil, you need to wind three or four thousand turns in total. This is nothing to comrades who have automatic counting winding machines, but we have to think about how many comrades have the above conditions? So to say that winding a coil of three or four thousand turns will give anyone a headache. Now there is the following method, comrades will not have a headache, because you only need to wind two thousand two hundred turns to get four hundred volts of "B" voltage, isn't this a very cheap thing! And the entire power transformer costs no more than four yuan at most, so it can be said to be extremely economical. First, let's talk about the transmitting part:

The circuit of the transmitter adopts screen-grid tuned (T.P.T.G.), which is easy to adjust and has stable frequency, which is most suitable for beginners to test. The grid circuit capacitor can be omitted (not shown in the figure) and replaced with a movable coil, so its frequency is still variable. The circuit of the transmitter is shown in Figure 1. All the parts used in the whole machine, except L1, L2, and L3, need to be made by yourself, and the rest are old goods removed from the radio. L1 and L2 are made of B.&S. No. 12 bare copper wire. (Note 1) Except for L3, L1 and L2 are wound with gaps, and the gap is equal to the diameter of the wire (ie 2.053 m.m). L1 is wound with six turns. The relationship between the number of turns of L2 and L3 and the frequency is detailed in the table below:

Coil Coil Diameter Number of Turns Frequency (K.C.) L2 21/2" 20 1750

L2 21/2" 8 3500

L2 21/2" 3 7000

L2 21/2 2 14000

L3 1" 150 1750

L3 1" 60 3500

L3 1" 25 7000

L3 1" 9 14000

In the figure, C4 is two 0.004 MFD fixed capacitors. Because they are radio-style and cannot withstand higher voltage, two are used in series here, and the voltage received by each is halved, so that there is no danger of short circuit. In addition, the circuit is simple, and there is no need to say more, everyone will know it: As for the adjustment of the transmitter, I think the readers must be much better than me, so I don't need to say it here. Let's talk about our power supply below.

This power supply can be divided into two parts, one part is the rectifier part (that is, "B" voltage), and the other part is the filament current supply. The entire power supply is supplied by four doorbell transformers. The author uses: domestic Ma brand doorbell transformer (of course, other brands are also available, but you must know that its input power is indeed 10 watts). Although the selling price of this transformer is the same, the goods are often different (Note 2), you must pay attention when buying. After the transformer is purchased, you can start the winding work. First, disassemble the transformer and remove all four secondary coils. The transformation method of T1 and T2 is the same, both use B.&S. No. 30 enameled wire to wind one thousand one hundred turns as the secondary coil of T1 and T2. (When winding, do not separate the first layer and the second layer with thicker insulation, for fear that it will take up too much space, so that the coil cannot be wound down) In application, you must use it in reverse, that is, the original primary is used as the current high-voltage secondary, and the original secondary is used as the current primary, but what you must pay attention to when connecting is: the two 1100-turn primaries (according to the current saying) are connected in series in the 220-volt circuit: the secondaries are connected in parallel. After the coil is wound, the original iron sheet can be inserted. There are gaps left in the iron sheet of this kind of transformer (for heat dissipation). Now when applying it, you must find some black iron sheet (most of the comrades who make transformers themselves will have this kind of black iron sheet. If there is emery steel sheet, it is even better), fill these air gaps to increase the cross-sectional area of the iron core. On the surface, it seems that you cannot use it as said above, because the original primary is two hundred and twenty volts, and the changed secondary is fifty-five volts, how can you connect the fifty-five volt secondary coil to a one hundred and ten volt circuit? The reason is that when manufacturers make doorbell transformers, the primary (two hundred and twenty volt coil) is always connected to the two hundred and twenty volt line, and the doorbell switch is connected in series in the secondary, so the number of turns in the primary is often more than what is usually calculated. Moreover, the cross-sectional area of the iron core is now doubled, so it is okay to connect its fifty-five volt coil to a one hundred and ten volt line.

After T1 and T2 are wound, you can start winding T3 and T4. The number of turns of these two is also the same (if 45 oscillation is used), both use B.&S. No. 16 enameled wire to wind fifty turns; T4 can also be wound with No. 18 wire, but for the convenience of purchase, you can use No. 16 for both. After the four transformers are wound, they can be connected according to the circuit in the second figure, and the entire transmitter is completed.

Parts used in the whole machine:

L1, L2, L3, the manufacturing method is detailed in the text.

C1¨·0005Mfd ordinary large 23-piece variable capacitor one

C2¨·00025Mfd fixed capacitor one

C3¨·006Mfd fixed capacitor two

C4¨·004Mfd fixed capacitor two

R1¨ depends on the vacuum tube used. If 75 is used, R1 should be 50000

R2¨ center-divided resistor, 20 when using 45

R·F·C· high-frequency choke coil used in ordinary radios

V1¨45 vacuum tube one

V2¨82 vacuum tube one

T1, T2, T3, T4¨ doorbell transformer four

A·F·C·30H, 60m·a· low-frequency choke coil one

C5¨2Mfd voltage-resistant 1000V· paper fixed capacitor two

Note 1: The reason why L1 and L2 use bare copper wire is (1) cheap. The copper wire used in several bands of this machine is less than half a catty in total. Compared with copper tube, the price of copper wire is tens to one. (2) Because the transmitting power is small, the efficiency of using copper tube and copper wire is almost the same, so it is more appropriate to use copper wire

Note 2: Not long ago, a friend bought this kind of transformer and tried it at home. Although it was not loaded (noload), it heated up by itself after about thirty or forty minutes, probably due to short circuit or EddyCurrent.

Characteristics of Short Wavelength 235

— Hua Xin

(1) Short wavelengths have excellent transmission efficiency.

(2) Short wavelengths have little absorption during transmission.

(3) Short wavelengths have almost no interference from atmospheric electricity.

(4) Small power and small antennas can be used for long-distance communication.

This point can be easily deduced from the characteristics of (1), (2), and (3). In fact, only a very small power of 5 watts to 10 watts can be used for very long-distance communication, and the amount of power is almost unrelated to the distance. What is related to long-distance communication is only the stability of the oscillation frequency.

(5) The communication wavelength band (frequency band) increases, and multiple communications can be performed at the same time.

(6) Directional communication is easy to implement.

The above points are the characteristics of short wavelengths, and its shortcomings are:

(7) Oscillation frequency is easy to change.

(8) Radio tuning is more difficult than long waves.

(9) Due to power limitations, it is inevitable to be disturbed by noise.

Shenbao Wireless Radio Weekly Department

Eight Trigram Tomb 236

— Chi Fo

Outside the west gate of my hometown, less than a mile away, there is a particularly large mound, towering up and covered with weeds, like a small mountain. This mound is octagonal, with each side paved with stone blocks, and it is impossible to tell which side is the front and which side is the back. Because it looks like the eight trigrams, the villagers call it "Eight Trigram Tomb."

It is said that the descendants of this Eight Trigram Tomb were very prosperous in the late Ming Dynasty, and they enjoyed wealth and glory. Because this Eight Trigram Tomb is shaped like a steamer, there were houses all around it, with smoke rising from the chimneys, resembling a steamer being heated up, with vigorous hot air. Therefore, the descendants of the Eight Trigram Tomb all prospered, becoming wealthy and glorious. In the Qing Dynasty, the residents next to the tomb all moved into the city to live, thus breaking the feng shui and cooling down the steamer; therefore, the descendants of the Eight Trigram Tomb all declined. That's what my friend said.

Oh! This is actually the tomb of Zhao Wenhua, who was very powerful during the Jiajing period of the Ming Dynasty and was attached to Yan Song. When Song was in power, he was called a powerful traitor. Although Zhao Wenhua was a member of Yan's party, he was very active in his hometown, such as building the county town and building Jia Yi Ting, and was willing to serve his hometown. Therefore, even though the villagers despise him, they still call him "Bright Traitor." They say he is a traitor, but his brain is not confused, and he is ultimately better than the current "Chinese traitors" and "traitorous merchants." That's what I said to my friend.

In less than four hundred years, Zhao Wenhua's descendants have truly declined to a regrettable state! Indeed, it is hard to find a few Zhao families in the entire county, and they are very poor. Now, near Nanmen, there are still two stone lions squatting outside Nanmu Hall. It is said that Nanmu Hall was Zhao Wenhua's old residence. Last year, I met a vagrant on ×× Road in Shanghai who was begging me pitifully. It is said that this vagrant is indeed a descendant of Zhao Wenhua. My friend said this to me again.

I couldn't help but sigh, and had no other reply.

Dog Racing Sketch 237

— Shen Yu

This place is a bottomless pit of money! It's a place of decadence! But the bourgeois young men and women, the big clerks of company foreign firms, the fat-bellied merchants with huge assets, the young masters and playboys who squander money like dirt, and those... all flock to it like ducks! Yes, they seem to have lost their souls! As if they have gone mad, as if on the eve of the earth's explosion, everyone is reveling and anesthetizing themselves here.

The dazzling "hua cha hua cha" of banknotes are competing to be stuffed into the hands of the person sitting on the high stool behind the counter, stuffed, stuffed, thus exchanging for red, yellow, green, and gray dog ​​tickets. When the bell rings, the electric rabbit rushes out of the wooden box and flies along the surrounding iron track. The group of dogs wearing "dog clothes" of different colors on their backs are chasing closely behind it. They are chasing, chasing, and thousands of eyes are all focused on them, emitting sparks of hope!

The lights judging the victory or defeat are on! The winners show a smug smile, and the losers show a frustrated look, and then throw away the dog ​​tickets. Then, the "hua cha hua cha" of banknotes are vying to be stuffed into the hands of the person behind the counter, stuffed, stuffed...

Like this, time after time, the "track owner's boss"'s pockets are stuffed full, full. However, on the other hand, a large number of people who seem to have lost their souls and were once crazy here, some are ruined! Some have become drifters on the street! Some have even committed suicide because of this! Some...

But after one group leaves, a new group comes. However, this new group will, in the near future, replace the previous group and become ruined, drifting, and suicidal. ...

Little Western Paradise 238

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Remote Place, Light Official, Far Away, Strong-Willed Order, Magnificent Hall Banquet, Outside There Are Pitiful Worms

Unexpectedly, as he was hesitating like this, the woman behind him sobbed and covered her face with her sleeve, crying. Naturally, Jie Fu couldn't help but be stunned. He was thinking that Zhu Yueying was a girl he greatly admired, so he shouldn't offend her. Under the moonlight, although he couldn't show a smiling face to others, he couldn't stand straight in front of them either. So, he slightly bent his waist and smiled, "What's wrong? Did my words scare you?" Yueying recognized him. Now that things had come to this, being shy was no longer an option. She turned her head, looked at him, and said, "This is my mother. No one has ever said such things to her. You, sir, keep pressing us to ask questions. She's too embarrassed and has to cry. Sir, she's a villager. Please have pity on her and don't force us." As she spoke, her voice couldn't help but become dry and she couldn't speak. Zhang Jiefu had never encountered such a thing before. He hadn't said a single harsh word, but he felt that every word he said was stabbing at people's hearts. He smiled and said, "Then you misunderstood me. Under the moonlight, I didn't know it was you two. Oh! Yes, I remembered something. Mr. Cheng wants to find something for you two to do. Did you know?" Although the woman had stopped crying, she didn't say anything and continued to rub her eyes with her sleeve. Yueying said, "Thank you, we already know." Jie Fu was left speechless by her reply. However, he felt guilty for having forced her to cry, so he said to her, "The people who are coming to eat haven't arrived yet. Even Mr. Cheng is still sitting in his own room. You're standing here waiting under the moonlight. When will you stop? Why don't you come to my room and sit for a while?" Yueying said, "No, my mother is afraid of people." Zhang Jiefu couldn't say anything more. After standing for a while, he resumed pacing back and forth under the moonlight with his hands behind his back. (129)

Record of Fleeting Fragrance from the Imperial Court 239

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Regardless of the truth of the matter, the Tongzhi Empress certainly took her own life. At the time of her suicide, she was almost ten months pregnant. The last bit of bloodline left by the Tongzhi Emperor perished with her. (Translator's note: The assertion that the Tongzhi Empress was pregnant is actually inaccurate. It was created out of indignation towards Cixi's despotism by people at the time who felt sorry for the Empress and deeply resented Cixi's autocracy, thus increasing Cixi's culpability. However, this claim also appears in "Empress Dowager Cixi: An Intimate History" by Englishman Backhouse, which many readers consider an anecdote.) Although no one knew whether the unborn child was a boy or a girl, if it had been a boy, the Tongzhi Empress would have been revered as Empress Dowager after his birth, and our Old Buddha [Cixi] would no longer have such a good position and such high authority. Therefore, the death of this unborn child along with his mother was truly a great advantage for the Old Buddha! Writing this, I can't help but think of four pitiful middle-aged women who live almost in another world, whom no one ever notices. Perhaps they cannot see anyone at all. Although they live with us in the palace, they are like prisoners, forever confined in a very secluded courtyard, never allowed to go outside all year round. I suspect that, except for death, they can no longer have any contact with the outside world. So, who are these women? They are the concubines of the Tongzhi Emperor. When the Tongzhi Emperor passed away, they were still young women with black hair and rosy cheeks. The Empress Dowager refused to let them out, but did not want to see them either, lest it arouse their sorrow for Tongzhi. Thus, she locked them up in the deep palace as if burying them alive, until this very day. (239)

The Stroke of Prince Guo's Pen 240

— China United Press

Prince Guo, the sixth son of the Kangxi Emperor of the late Qing Dynasty and younger brother of the Yongzheng Emperor, toured Sichuan and Kang areas in the fourth year of Yongzheng's reign. He resided in Dajianlu for about ten years, and then took the daughter of the Ming Zheng Tusi (local chieftain) as his concubine. It is said that the Tusi of various places in Xikang are all descendants of Prince Guo. The Tusi of Xikang are mostly of the Jia and Mu surnames. Some say that splitting the character "Guo" (果) into two yields those characters, thus asserting they are descendants of Prince Guo. Because Yongzheng cruelly killed his brothers, Prince Guo dared not return to the capital and stayed in Xikang until Yongzheng passed away, when he returned to court to report. When the news of Yongzheng's death reached Xikang, Prince Guo observed mourning and slept on grass in Lijiang County. Therefore, Yajiang still has the Wolong Stone (Sleeping Dragon Stone), which is a relic of that time. Prince Guo lived in Kang for a long time and knew the customs and conditions of the people well. His work, "The Stroke of the Pen," describes the customs of Xikang in great detail. Here we explore and record it to show a general picture of Xikang customs.

(1) Wandering thousands of miles, going west out of the furnace pass to the end of the sky, the mountain path is majestic and steep, the sound of the water is ferocious and roaring, willow branches sprout in April, there are no splendid flowers, only mad winds, regardless of dusk or dawn. Therefore, I strike out all the colorful splendor with a single stroke.

(2) Entering and exiting on fine steeds, accustomed to being lords of ten thousand households in the emperor's house, generations inheriting great favor, with official hats and belts passed down to sons and grandsons; meritorious deeds inscribed on Lingge pavilion, glory and wealth is enough, why bother holding scriptures to walk towards the literary arena? Therefore, I strike out the golden list of successful candidates with a single stroke.

(3) Shapeless sheepskin robe, always worn in all seasons, never discarded, white snow piles up thick on the mountains, cool breeze penetrates in midsummer: no need to seek gauze and Ge (coarse cloth), durable , a small bell rings, hanging on the chest, therefore, I strike out the brocade and silk with a single stroke.

(4) Head of a Ke Yao family, tea boiled with milk is offered in a bowl, highland barley wine from the barbarians, Zanba (roasted highland barley flour) and ghee; beef legs and mutton elbows, eaten with the fur, a whirlwind sweeps, eaten until nothing is left, therefore, I strike out delicacies from land and sea with a single stroke.

(5) Barbaric and remote frontier, people live in hundred-foot buildings, dogs of bereaved families everywhere, the smell of feces and urine fills the house, walls are piled with messy stones, colored flags in front and behind, a golden-topped flagpole, standing alone to the right of the door, therefore, I strike out painted beams and carved pillars with a single stroke. (The remaining two songs are omitted.)

Record of Martial Arts Tuina Practitioner Jin Wentao 241

— Zhang Zhenlu

Our country has always valued literature and belittled martial arts, resulting in a weak and declining nation. Only a few ambitious people are willing to study, invent, practice, and teach martial arts. Because our country has been civilized for a long time, the achievements of martial arts are more profound and magnificent than those of other countries. Even in this era when our country is inferior to others in many ways, a Russian strongman came to Beijing to show off his skills, calling himself invincible in the world, but he was scared away by a Chinese woman named Yang who came from a remote rural area, which can be regarded as a consolation. It is a pity that there are martial artists with great skills in our country, existing like rare treasures, very few in number, unable to spread widely and cultivate a national spirit of martial valor, merely serving as something for people to marvel at their strange abilities after drinking and tea, creating an impression similar to myths!

Here, I am recording a martial artist named Jin Wentao. He is a Muslim and originally engaged in the jewelry business, traveling to and from Shanghai and Guangdong for many years, and also going abroad several times to Java and the South Seas, selling cheap and buying dear, his fate rising and falling repeatedly. However, when he was fourteen or fifteen years old, he unintentionally met an old man named Sha, who was also a Muslim, who taught him various martial arts. He devoted ten years of hard work to it before he felt he had achieved some success. Mr. Jin's work of sitting in meditation every night continues to this day without interruption: he sleeps very little, often using meditation instead of sleep, and his spirit is particularly strong. He never knew his master's name, only calling him Master Sha. He often provided financial assistance to his master until he saw his master's death, handling the funeral and mourning, because Old Man Sha had no family or close relatives, nor any other disciples. This also shows the strangeness of his master's origin and the beauty of the meeting between these two disciples!

Although Mr. Jin is skilled in martial arts, his appearance is very refined, and he also works in the business world. Even those who are close to him on a daily basis do not know that he possesses martial arts skills. He himself is deeply hidden, unwilling to reveal his abilities in front of others. Even so, more than a decade ago, someone would come from afar to visit him, saying they sought instruction out of admiration. After he repeatedly declined and pleaded to be excused, he had no choice but to approach the visitor with a humble attitude and sparred with him in a secluded location. After only a few exchanges, he kicked the visitor to the ground, defeating him and sending him away.

After middle age, Mr. Jin grew weary of the travels and hardships of business and settled in Shanghai. Some people advised him to set up a school and teach students, but he said, "I still have some other skills to make a living, which are more beneficial than teaching martial arts." Therefore, he practiced medicine using Tuina massage. Now he is still located inside the alley diagonally opposite the Yunnan Road Hot Spring Bathhouse, to serve those who are ill.

The Short Selling Camp is Extremely Firm

Final Drop of Eleven Yuan and Seven Jiao

Yesterday, due to the sharp weakening of foreign exchange during the Lunar New Year holiday and the extremely firm position of the short selling camp, the gold market suffered a miserable plunge due to downward sentiment. However, there was sudden support after the drop, and eager short covering, resulting in a mediocre situation. During the Spring Festival holiday, overseas silver markets rose across the board. Imported Wheat Affects the Flour Market, Wheat Plummets 253

Yesterday, in the flour market, after opening in the morning, the market for all months showed a uniform sharp decline. The price of imported wheat, since the market closure, has fallen nearly six jiao in Chicago and two to four jiao for distant months, and about two and a half jiao in Canada (it has rebounded on the 7th). When pricing, the price of imported wheat naturally made people nervous, and the combined price of spot imported wheat is still cheap. Various factories are purchasing one after another due to demand. It is heard that another ship of Australian wheat was ordered the day before yesterday at a price of 4.82 yuan. As for the various road merchant groups, because they are in the early stages of disaster relief, they have little interest in purchasing. Therefore, the market atmosphere is slack, and various factories are selling off, causing prices for all months to fall step by step. Considering the current trend of imported wheat and the continued tight money supply, there is little hope for a rebound in the future. As a result, the price for this month fell by four fen, March by five fen seven li and a half, April by six fen two li and a half, May by five fen seven li and a half, June by four fen and a half, and July initially opened at four jiao four fen seven li and a half, and closed at four jiao one fen, also a decrease of three fen seven li and a half. Furthermore, the flour exchange will only operate for half a day in the morning from the 8th to the 13th, and will resume normal operations from the 14th onwards.

Yesterday, in the wheat futures market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, the market for all months showed a uniform sharp decline. The price of imported wheat fell by two to four and six jiao in Chicago and about two jiao in Canada. When the market opened in the morning, with the decline in prices of imported wheat futures and the continued selling of spot imported wheat, and given the current situation where the price of imported wheat is still cheaper than local wheat, many external bulls sold off as soon as the market opened, and the market plummeted endlessly. When the market opened in the afternoon, due to the sluggishness of the flour market and a portion of imported wheat being hedged, the market atmosphere remained depressed. Transactions were brisk in all contracts. Considering the recent trend, with continuous orders for imported wheat, there is little hope for a rebound. As a result, the price for this month fell by one jiao two fen, March by one jiao six fen, and April by one jiao four fen. Spot wheat saw no trading yesterday due to inactive factory demand.

The settlement of long positions in overseas Chicago wheat has been abundant, and there were slightly more purchases today, but the exchange's open interest is the smallest since July of last year.

"Yuanbao Business" of the Woolen Cloth Group 260

The Market is Adorned, Transactions Have Not Yet Begun

Yesterday, being the fifth day of the Lunar New Year, the woolen cloth industry welcomed the God of Wealth and opened the market at 1:00 AM. Sellers successively prepared samples and opened their stalls. Salesmen and brokers went out to solicit business. Buyers, out of courtesy, mostly selected and matched purchases as a token of support. This kind of initial transaction at the beginning of the year is referred to by both parties as "Yuanbao Business." For the most part, the prices were equal to the closing prices of last year. Because in recent days, the association's standard prices have not yet been agreed upon, buying and selling must still wait.

North-South Goods Prices, Key North-South Goods Rise 261

But Actual Sales are Still Stagnant

Yesterday, the prices of North-South goods were negotiated and finalized. Most of them showed an increase. Among the South goods, Jinshan branches saw a greater increase. For example, glutinous rice branches increased by 30 to 40 yuan due to land prices. Round and flat branches also increased by 4-5 yuan to nearly 10 yuan. Dried longan increased by 1-2 yuan. Screened longan, except for the top grade, was mostly stagnant, while medium and small grades increased by 2-3 yuan. Among the North goods, the main goods also generally increased. Daylily increased by 1-2 yuan, Xiang lotus increased by 3-4 yuan, White lotus increased by 2-3 yuan, Wood ear increased by 5-6 yuan, Peach kernel walnuts increased by 3-4 yuan, Black melon seeds increased by 0.4-0.5 yuan, Top-grade pressed fruit increased by about 1 yuan, and the bottom grades saw little change. The remaining red and black dates, vermicelli, and other items saw more stable price changes. However, actual sales have not yet moved significantly. Whether the rising trend can be stable still depends on the rise and fall of demand. Yesterday, the market only saw sporadic transactions. Among the dried longan firms, He Feng, De Feng, and three or four others closed. There may be one or two more closing or changing owners. Among the North goods firms, there were four or five closures or reorganizations. Only a small number made a profit, mainly because last year, with the collapse of the rural economy, business was reduced and there were not many opportunities to profit.

Hardware: Hardware Red Opening Higher Than Last Year 262

The hardware red market prices were officially opened yesterday. The agreed-upon prices were all raised by several jiao to one or two yuan compared to last year's market prices, so it is expected that future transactions will inevitably be affected. The tight money supply and the desolation of the market are undeniable facts. If you don't find ways to promote sales and just think about the interests of one side, there will be no good results. Oil Market: Chaos in Both Shanghai and Hankou for Winter Cypress Oil 263

The cypress oil production this winter was the lowest in western Zhejiang, and although eastern Zhejiang was slightly better, it was still not as good as previous years. The initial news from the Jingyi area of western Hubei was that it was a bumper harvest, but after verification, it was also lower than in the past. Therefore, all cypress oil production areas reported poor harvests, and the number of cypress oil produced was reduced considerably. Therefore, no area had a feeling of lack of oil in the winter supply. The most severe shortage was in this port. In previous years, we relied entirely on Zhejiang cypress oil. And Jiaxing, in western Zhejiang, is the closest to Shanghai, and the supplies arrived in the evening of the day they were dispatched, but because the harvest this winter was only 30%, there was concern that even local sales would not be sufficient, and there was no excess oil to be shipped to Shanghai. In addition, oil from Wenzhou and Taizhou also did not sell far because the price in the production area was too high. The Chen oil had run out in Jiangxi Province and the new oil also was only supplying local areas, so the sources on which this port relied were all cut off. Therefore, from the time the new crop was produced until the final settlement, only a few hundred pieces arrived. As a result, the lack of oil this winter was unprecedented. Moreover, before the end of the year, a certain soap factory purchased a large quantity in Hankou, causing the stocks in both Hankou and Shanghai to be extremely sparse. It is feared that the opening price of spring cypress oil from Jingyi will be above 21 yuan per piece.
