Free Talk

Shoveling Away the Coal Slag 281

— Hu Luo

The burning in a furnace, after a certain period, shows signs of decline. At this time, the bottom layer of coal slag should be removed, and some new, black and shiny pieces of coal should be added. Thus, the furnace becomes hot and vigorous again.

Literature is the same, shining with different splendor from era to era. When a society transforms into another society, two different kinds of literature are produced in society: one is energetic and upward; the other is decadent and downward. The former is the newly added coal, which is emitting a red glow; the latter is just the coal that is about to burn out, gradually losing its flames. Its result is coal slag, and this coal slag will inevitably suffer the fate of being shoveled away. In the early days of Romanticism, it was a burning piece of coal, and we could see that great, extraordinary, and sharp flame. Victor Hugo shouted in "Hernani": "Ah, the people! The ocean! The surging waves! ··· This wave that destroys thrones and shakes tombs!" However, the burning of coal will gradually disappear, and it will change from a red-hot flame to a dim light, and then become coal slag. The evolution of society also causes the "furnace" of literature to form a state of metabolism. Romantic literature will inevitably lead to Naturalism. At the same time, their youthful enthusiasm and flames gradually disappeared. They "want to escape from their era and go to the ideal realm of the past era (especially the Middle Ages), or the abstraction of life, as a place of concealment" (in the words of Iakovlevich). Thus, Realism became the negation of Romanticism and became the newly added coal, burning again in the furnace. Romanticism became coal slag and had to be shoveled away.

When a certain society is changing, new coal and coal that is about to become coal slag both exist in the "furnace" of literature. At this time, coal slag certainly has its inevitable fate of sinking, but it is still struggling and hindering the progress of the furnace fire from time to time. Sometimes, too much coal slag will dim the furnace fire, and even extinguish it temporarily. Therefore, in the progress of the times, the role of coal slag is to hinder the evolution of society. For the sake of the future of society, it is really necessary to shovel away the coal slag. However, some people still say: "Those literatures that are about to become coal slag are not our enemies. Instead of attacking them, we should appease them." Isn't this defending coal slag? Of course, coal slag also has its historical value. However, when coal slag hinders the prosperity of the furnace fire, we can only seriously attack and criticize them. In today's society, the low-level Saturday School novels are still popular, as are the multi-angle love novels, and there are even novels that specialize in writing about dancers, circuses, and decadence. But, undeniably, these are all coal slag! Coal slag is dimming the light of the furnace fire. For the sake of the future of literature, we must not only attack and criticize them, but also strive to shovel them out of the furnace, and even use water to extinguish their remaining flames!

We also know that there are many new, black, and shiny pieces of coal waiting to be lit. Only these new pieces of coal can make the furnace fire of literature burn hotter and redder!

"Collection of Purchased Sorrows" 282

— Zai Qing

Qian Shangying (Zhenzhi), self-titled Master of Suishan, historical details unknown. I once saw his essays "Collection of Purchased Sorrows" in four volumes, mostly based on the poems and lyrics of his predecessors, slightly referencing historical facts, or completely from imagination, evolving into novels, mostly two hundred characters long, and sometimes only dozens of words. Each volume has a preface engraved in his own handwriting, and a foreword. When I borrowed the book from a friend, I selected and copied two excerpts. One of them said: "When Jie Xisi was not yet successful, he traveled between Hunan and Xiang. One day, he moored his boat on the bank of the river. At the second watch of the night, he put on his clothes and sat outside, looking up at the bright moon as if it were daytime. Suddenly, a boat in the middle of the river gradually approached, and a woman in plain dress stood up, very elegant in appearance. Jie Xisi asked her, and she said, I am a merchant's wife. My husband has not returned for a long time. I heard that you were coming, so I came to greet you. So he talked with her, and they were very happy. Until dawn, he was reluctant to leave. He gave Jie Xisi a poem, saying, 'My family is on the Pantang River, come and have tea if you have time; the walls are made of yellow earth and the roof is covered with thatch, and there is a tree of purple lilac in front of the courtyard.' The next day, the boat was blocked by the wind, so he went ashore to buy wine. When he asked about it, it was Pantang Town. After walking a few steps, he saw a house with walls and a courtyard full of purple lilacs. A young boy was standing under the flowers. When he asked him, he said that the head of the family was away on a long journey, and his wife lived alone, and died after being ill for three years, and was buried in the back garden yesterday. Xisi went to see it and saw that the purple lilacs in front of the tomb were very lush. Xisi wandered around and couldn't help but wet the tomb with tears."

The second one is based on Cui Hu's peach blossom poem. In the entire collection, it is the best one. The text says: "Cui Hu initially failed to pass the imperial examination, and traveled alone to the south of the capital during the Qingming Festival, and found a village house with clusters of flowers and trees. Hu knocked on the door for a long time, and a woman asked him from the crack in the door. He replied: I am looking for spring alone, and I am thirsty for wine. The woman opened the door and brought a bowl of water. She leaned alone on the young peach tree and seemed to have deep affection. Cui said goodbye and sent her to the door, as if she could not bear it, and then went in. He never came again. By the time of Qingming the following year, he went straight to find her, but the door was already locked. So he inscribed a poem on the left door: 'Last year today in this door, peach blossoms reflected the red faces. Where have the faces gone now? The peach blossoms still smile in the spring breeze.'" "I don't know where the face is," here it is written as "the faces now", I don't know if it is based on another version, or if it is Shanghao's memory error.

Occasionally, he also reprinted other people's long works, such as Tu Long's "The Journey of Mingliaozi", this book transcribed the entire upper part. The one about Tie Xuan's daughter also differs greatly from the one recorded in "One Hundred Novelists". According to this record, it is said that "Tie Xuan was a chief administrator, and died for his country during the Jingnan rebellion. Both of his daughters were of national beauty. [Unreadable] was furious and ordered them to enter the Jiaofang. After several days of hard work, they vowed not to be humiliated. At that time, a colleague of Xuan's arrived, and the two daughters presented a poem to him," I don't know who is reliable. This book can be said to be a unique work in the notes of novels, but unfortunately there are not many good ones. The Ming carved version I saw has a good layout and font, but unfortunately there are many typos, I don't know if it was the owner's first carving.

Sedan Chair 283

— Lu Fen

丨A Retrospective of Daxing丨

Going to the mountains in the rain is a kind of happiness, although sometimes it has its drawbacks.

That day, the rain was the kind that "refreshes the willows with green, like a traveler's inn," though I knew I wasn't exactly heading out of Yangguan Pass, I was still filled with longing. Perhaps it was a bit romantic. The name Daxing initially sounded a bit intimidating. Naturally, this was likely related to the old novels I had read. But let's not dwell on that.

Daxing Mountain, with such a resounding name, should itself be magnificent. It was hard to say whether this trip would bring extraordinary encounters. For example, heroes and immortals. Just hearing about them was enough to surprise people. (Back then) Grand floods, Shaolin, and two-hundred-year-old monks were showing off everywhere! So, without any preparation, I asked the host to call for a vehicle. Because I had nothing on me, not even needing to pack, I set off. It was truly very simple.

The driver was an elderly man nearing seventy, said to be an "expert" in this profession for decades. The vehicle was what they call a "sedan chair," often appearing in "The Travels of Lao Can"; southerners probably lack this sight, but there are plenty in the north. However, in recent years, it has been declining. Some places have already replaced it with cars and rickshaws. Although there are still quite a few in remote areas, they are just waiting for "time" to include them in history. The vehicle is called a sedan, but it is not a sedan. Apart from the wooden shaft of the carriage, you can't find any similarities. The vehicle has two wheels, with a diameter of about three feet, which is much more advanced than the "Taiping cart" and the hand-pushed wheelbarrow that can also run on the same track. It has a canopy, arched, covered with a curtain, much like the bamboo awning of a small boat in landscape paintings, only smaller. So no one drinks wine and enjoys the moon inside, which is a pity. The reason it's called a sedan chair, I think, is probably because it once showed off in officialdom, because the character is simpler than sedan, and it only needs to be hitched to a mule. It doesn't necessarily require four people to carry it. Moreover, that two-foot wide and three-foot long compartment, to be comfortable, can only be occupied by one person, which ordinary people can't afford. In addition, there are two positions outside the canopy. The "inside (i.e., left) position" belongs to the driver; the "outside position," also known as the "shaft," naturally belongs to the "second master" carrying the "visiting card box."

When this vehicle is heavily loaded, it needs two to three animals to pull it. If it's just carrying people, it usually only hitches a strong mule. The one I was in was the latter, a "single shaft." According to the locals, the most extravagant is a "double set," which is a moderate approach, but I don't think so. Look, if there is a follower on the "shaft," doesn't that look like a reserve official? As for needing a "double set," that already indicates retirement.

Fine rain was falling. A layer of oilcloth had been added outside the curtain, so guests didn't have to worry. The vehicle was moving on the damp, loamy road. The driver "hee-hawed" while urging the trained mule, and the mule was truly trained. No matter what, it never ran a step. When the whip struck, it would just shake its big ears unhappily, and a "trot-trot" sound would come from its nose, and it would go unhurriedly. This is very suitable for people who have no urgent business to attend to, and they can take this opportunity to browse the scenery along the way.

The distant mountains were hidden in the mist. Nearby small ridges and low hills undulated in the rain. By the roadside, water droplets condensed on the wheat fields, like celestial robes covered with pearls. The villages were misty. The green willows contained smoke. It was around the time of Qingming Festival, very suitable for having a Xinghua Village to buy wine. There was no trace of people on the road, which was very desolate. If it were a writer, he might as well ponder it. Unfortunately, my mind was dry, and I had no ability to mend the sky, and I couldn't squeeze out a bit of "poetic juice." Never mind, leave it to later generations. Fortunately, we don't lack "vague" poets.

The driver and his trained mule were so refined that they bored me. The vehicle rattled all the way, and I was already dizzy from the shaking. It seemed like it was still far from the station, and there was no rushing it, so I fell asleep. I don't know if I missed this ready-made picture in my sleep, but when I was awakened by the driver's scolding, the situation was very different. Although the sky was still covered with thin clouds, the rain had stopped. The small hills were even more cumbersome and trivial, and the main vein of Daxing was already in sight.

The driver stopped the vehicle, went to a stone house by the roadside to get tinder, and asked about the route. Only then did I realize that this old "expert" was not so expert after all, at least he still had to ask people for directions on this road. This road was originally a convenient route to Shanxi. The so-called convenient route means it's between a highway and a small path. At this time, several passengers had come down from the mountain, some with "shoulder poles" and some with loads, mostly agricultural products to be sold "down below." There was also wine from Shanxi.

The vehicle's next journey was terrible. The road was full of rocks, and the mule kept slipping and falling. It was not walking, but climbing. Sometimes the driver had to go down to hold it. As for the vehicle, it was simply a rickety skeleton. It rattled and shook all over, and sometimes it even showed off its martial arts, jumping to the side of the road with a "Kangcha" sound. You had to watch your head. By the time we reached the foot of the mountain, the birds had returned to their nests and the dogs were barking. It was almost dusk.

The Celebrated Jumping Frog (3) 284

— Translated by Li Bo, written by Mark Twain

Smiley had rat-terriers, chicken-cocks, cats, and all sorts of things, and you couldn't keep up with them. If you took something to bet with him, he could always match you. One day, he caught a frog, took it home, and said he was going to educate it. So, for three months, he did nothing but sit in his backyard, teaching that frog to jump. And I could bet that he was really teaching it. He would give it a little tap from behind, and the next moment, you could see it spinning in the air like a doughnut, flipping a somersault, maybe two if the angle was good. Then it would land flat on its feet, unharmed. He taught it to catch flies and kept it practicing. As long as it saw a fly, it could catch it. Smiley said that the most important thing for a frog was education, and it could do almost anything – I believed him. Oh, I had seen him bring Dan'l Webster here – that was the frog's name – and put it on the floor, calling, "Flies, Dan'l, flies!" And before you could bat an eye, it would jump straight up, land on that counter over there, grab a fly, and then, as solid as a clod of earth, plop back down to the floor and start scratching the side of its head with its hind leg, as nonchalant as if it hadn't done anything more than a frog should do. You never saw a frog so modest and straightforward, even though it was such a genius. When it was given a fair start on a flat surface, it could jump better than any of its kind you ever saw. Jumping on a flat surface was its specialty, you know; if there was such a competition, Smiley would bet as much as he could afford. Smiley was extraordinarily proud of his frog, and he was right to be, because travelers from all over said it was superior to any frog they had ever seen.

Smiley kept this creature in a small square box and often took it to town to bet with people. One day, a stranger, a passerby in this area, came across him carrying this box and said to him,

"What's in that box of yours?"

Smiley, looking very indifferent, said, "Well, it might be a parrot, or it might be a canary, but it's neither – it's just a frog."

The man took the box, examined it carefully, and said, "Oh, that's it. So, what's it good for?"

"Well," Smiley said casually, without a care, "it's good for something, I'm sure – it can out-jump any frog in Calaveras County."

Farm Woman 285

— Chen Fuxi

"Mother Tian, your chickens are getting bigger!"

"Are they getting bigger?"

Hearing people say that the chickens are getting bigger, Mother Tian is very happy. She likes raising chickens. The chicks she raises every year are all hatched from her own hens, and the breed is bigger than "oven-baked chickens." Chicks hatched by hens can be sold for four hundred coins each in town, and people in town like to buy them, saying that these chicks grow easily and don't die easily. Chickens sell for a good price, but Mother Tian never cares about these three or four hundred coins. She is happy to see her own hen hatch chicks. If you ask her to sell them, Mother Tian can't bear to part with them, so she never sells her chicks. For seven or eight months, Mother Tian feeds them all day, manages the chicken coop, and watches out for wild dogs. She is almost always paying attention to these chickens.

"Mother Tian, your chickens are getting bigger!"

Hearing people say this makes her happy. Sometimes she even catches the chickens and weighs them in front of people:

"Five days ago, this speckled chicken weighed two catties and three taels. Now it weighs six taels more."

Mother Tian's face is full of smiles when she weighs them.

Mother Tian loves chickens so much that she is more devoted than people who love dogs, flowers, or birds. One year, she raised more than twenty young chickens, and five of them were bitten to death by weasels. That morning, after finding five dead chickens at the entrance of the chicken coop, Mother Tian started to cry. Other people tried to persuade her, but she couldn't be consoled. After that, she wouldn't feel at ease even going to bed unless she personally closed the chicken coop door.

Once the new chickens reached the winter solstice, the males would crow, and the females would already be able to lay eggs. Mother Tian loves raising chickens and also likes the eggs that the chickens lay. From the day the chickens start laying eggs, Mother Tian can pick up eggs in the chicken coop every day. She puts them in jars and doesn't sell them unless she needs money. Although Mother Tian loves raising chickens and works hard to raise them until they lay eggs and crow, she never eats chicken meat except for a few eggs. She raises the chicks as if she were raising her own children and doesn't want to slaughter them. She would rather sell them to other people at the end of the year for the New Year.

At the end of the year, Mother Tian's family is always more strapped for cash than usual. She has no money, so she has to go to town to sell chickens. Every year, she only leaves two hens to prepare for hatching eggs next spring, and sells all the rest.

"We're out of oil and salt..."

Mother Tian worries.

"What about rice?" her husband asks.

"It's almost gone too. There's only..."

"Then sell chickens tomorrow!"

Every time Mother Tian hears these words, it's like cutting her heart and liver. She feels that her husband is a cruel and cold person. But for the sake of oil and rice, Mother Tian can't care about the chickens. She has to let her husband tie up the chickens' feet and take them to town to sell for money.

"Ooooooo..."

The chickens with their feet tied up cry.

Hearing the chickens' tragic cries, Mother Tian's heart trembles painfully. Like the tears of mourning for the dead, they hang from her deep eye sockets onto her cheeks.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

An Examination of the Psychology of Peace and War 287

— Long

The Tokyo Asahi Shimbun carried a dispatch from its New York correspondent stating that the weekly magazine Literary Review and the University News Association conducted a vote to understand the psychology of American students regarding the current world situation. The results showed that out of 32,500 votes, the majority favored peace.

To be honest, this kind of psychological examination can be said to be superfluous. Because the psychology of hoping for peace can be said to be shared by all beings with blood and qi. Those who advocate war and do not hope for peace are only a small number of ambitious individuals and a group of militarists who specialize in reckless lawlessness and disregard everything.

Therefore, if you want to examine the psychology of peace and war, not only will the results of American students be like this, but the results of non-student examinations will also be the same. Not only in the United States, but even in Germany and Japan, which are currently eager for success, if you examine the psychology of ordinary people, the results will be the same.

Therefore, the psychology of war and peace does not need to be examined. However, this psychological examination of American students has deeper and more complex significance. There are five questions in the examination, the most important of which are the following three: 1. Will the United States be able to avoid being involved in the whirlpool of war in the future? The results showed that the majority believed that they would be involved in the whirlpool of war. 2. If the United States is invaded by other countries, are you willing to take up arms and fight? The majority agreed. 3. Should we invade other countries? Or should we not invade other countries? The majority argued that we should not invade other countries.

The first question is whether the United States should join a possible second world war in the future. The current result is that the majority advocates joining, which seems inconsistent with the psychology of loving peace. However, we must know that the current world is a world of power. If we love peace but do not join, the next step is that the god of war will descend on our own heads. The so-called "killing to stop killing" is also a method that peace-loving people must take. The so-called "sitting at home behind closed doors, disaster comes from the sky," the inapplicability of the Monroe Doctrine to the present world, its trend can be seen in general.

Should the United States take up arms to resist if invaded by other countries? 2. Should the United States invade other countries? Or should it not invade other countries? 3. Such questions do not need to be asked of students with clear intellect. Even if you ask children two or three feet tall, they will definitely answer crisply "take up arms and fight" and "should not invade." Why is this? This is called a universal principle and humanity of the human race. Assuming that this point is obliterated and acted in reverse, although it may not be impossible to show strength for a time, the result will eventually lead to failure. Even if it does not fail, it will only be a country that destroys humanity and destroys public morality, and will never be condoned.

Festivals 288

— Family Member

The situation is obviously very different from before.

In the past, whenever a festival was coming, people welcomed it with very joyful hearts. Everyone was busy preparing for the festival a few days in advance. And on the day of the festival, everyone was especially happy to celebrate the festival. At the same time, everyone also invited a few like-minded friends to get together and have fun drinking. It felt like every festival was the best time to relax and enjoy oneself.

And every shop was crowded with people. The shop assistants were too busy to handle it all. The boss sat in the back of the counter, smiling and stroking his beard. Even along the street, there were layers upon layers of fish vendors' stalls, and people surged back and forth like a tide. When they went out, their hands were empty, but when they came back, everyone was carrying a load of festival goods.

Now, this kind of lively scene has disappeared.

Although the fish vendors' stalls are still laid out all over the street as usual, the shops are still open as usual, and people are still bustling and coming and going as usual. But people's expressions are different. They are all gloomy, as if they will never see a smile. The shops are deserted, with few people. The shop assistants are bored, and the boss is no longer smiling, but is irritable and frowning, and sighing from time to time. The fish vendors' stalls have no business for half a day, and every customer seems to have suddenly become stingy, arguing about the price even for half a copper coin. As a result, they often run away.

—— The year is not good! It's getting worse every day.

The shop owners and the fish vendor owners both sighed at the same time.

The pedestrians on the street are equally crowded, but most of them are just going out to stroll around with their eyes, and returning home empty-handed.

—— Celebrate the festival!

—— Celebrate what festival? It's simply getting through a difficult time.

The voices that were spoken in the past were loud and clear, but now they are low and carry a hint of desolation. In the past, everyone was happy to mention it when they met someone, but now, not only does no one want to mention it, they are even afraid of hearing this voice. In the past, they wanted to buy more things to celebrate the festival, but now they are planning how to save money. It would be even better if they could save it all. When the festival is near, many debts are pressing at the same time. Everyone's heads are dreaming of gold day and night. However, everyone has no livelihood, no income at all. But they have to take care of eating and drinking every day, which has already made them unable to straighten their backs. Add to that the burden of the festival, and they can't even breathe.

Beaten by the pain of reality, life is getting harder and harder every day, and they are feeling the attacks of life with panicked hearts. When a festival comes, people's hearts become tense, struggling to barely get through it. They take a breath, and then there is another festival following closely behind. Countless festivals are forever threatening people with fierce and merciless terror.

Lonely Years 289

— Dani

Living in loneliness, twenty lonely winters have sent away my youth.

Living in the near suburbs of the city, two lonely companions lived together; but in the autumn of falling leaves, my lonely friend left me. Accustomed to living a lonely life, I welcome this twenty-first lonely winter.

What my friend left behind here is a photograph of us together.

I glanced at him habitually - we can communicate our thoughts in loneliness, move the rattan armchair to the side of the stove, and brew a pot of Longjing tea. I close my eyes driftingly, as if my lonely companion is sitting opposite me; shaking his legs, chewing the taste of Turkish tobacco, the blazing flames kiss me, and I am misty pulled back to the season when chrysanthemums are in full bloom.

(Let's toast our newly added lonely comrades, finish this cup!

From then on, brilliant flowers bloomed in this lonely cellar. A clinging little bird shook our two lonely hearts.

In the morning, facing the golden sunlight, we waved goodbye at the bus stop, and the heavy work seemed to be lightened. Facing the golden sunlight again, we returned with smiling faces. We cooked fragrant rice on the gas stove, made various dishes by hand, and made life light and comfortable.

On nights when the bright moon was overhead, we stepped on our long shadows, blocked the autumn wind, and roamed the banks of the nearby small river. Or we rented a small boat and boating under the moon, and sent away the twenty lonely years like my youth.)

Dream!

Throwing away the cigarette butts, savoring the bitter Turkish taste, the two lonely companions are sitting opposite each other in the photo.

"When you were attached to the little bird in your arms, did you ever raise your glass to toast the lonely old comrades?"

I am lonely facing it, naturally it is a lonely answer!

A burst of trivial sounds rang out, it was two beads hitting the glass window, it played moving music with the flames in the stove. Drinking Longjing tea, I smiled victoriously; people who make a living in loneliness have long been deprived of that kind of light and comfortable day!

Slowly, the glass window became covered with mist, and the clanging sound seemed to fade away gradually. There is no moonlight in the sky, I don't know what kind of world is a piece of misty black night?

The lonely rainy alley, send a sob of singing, is it a lilac girl?

"It's the bitter old man who died of his daughter! The lonely companion said softly in my ear.

Really! That day we came back from boating, we saw him playing a hoarse erhu alone, singing Meng Jiangnu's song "The first month is the New Year" in a false voice.

Page 20

He told us that his companion – a lilac-like girl – had died, and selling songs alone was lonely and not doing good business!

Our little bird pitied him and sent him two dimes, saying: "Old man, buy a dime of beef and a dime of wheat wine to spend this lonely night!"

Now, this bitter old man has also added a lonely winter, singing Meng Jiangnu's song in a false voice. I want to push open the window and ask him if he has met the little girl who gave him two dimes? However, in this cold wind and rain, can you bear to listen to the hoarse erhu and the song "The first month is the New Year"?

Leaning my head on the back of the rattan chair, I lit a cigarette. The blazing stove and bitter Longjing have been occupied by me, in your lonely life it is enough to be proudly in front of that bitter old man, he is living through twice as lonely years as you!

I smiled victoriously again!

Having Gold Ingots But No Food to Eat 290

Riverside Night Talk 291

— Ke Ming

The boat entered the inner river, it was dusk: a very thick fog had risen, and ships could not be seen five feet away. The boatman was cautious, saying that they could have arrived before the lanterns were lit, but now that such a thick fog had risen outside, they couldn't see anyone across from them, so who would dare to be so bold as to sail out and collide with other boats? He said it was a matter of everyone's lives, and they might as well rest for the night and leave at daybreak.

And so, we all had to spend the night on the boat.

Listening to the echoing shouts, the boatman secured the ropes firmly; then he gathered firewood to make a fire and cook dinner. It was completely dark, and the river surface was shrouded in a layer of thick fog. Lanterns were scattered sparsely everywhere, like torches behind a beaded curtain, hazy and charming. Usually, boats gathered in groups of three or five. We could hear the boatmen chatting and sighing across the boats, and the noise of chickens, dogs, and children. From the shore came the sounds of people, the sounds of hawking, and the sounds of vehicles and horses. Through the thick fog, we could still vaguely see the outlines of houses and softened lamplight. The world was deathly still, and the vast river surface was also deathly still, but across the dividing line, it nurtured a kind of melancholy, a kind of despondency, a kind of aloofness and loneliness.

A breeze stirred on the river, slowly. The old boatman brought the steaming hot rice into the cabin, with a cautious, reverent expression, let the guests eat their fill, and then went to the bow of the boat with his companions and children to eat.

The night wind made people shiver, and the night was also quite boring. The passengers in the cabin asked the boatmen to clear away the remains of dinner, and some, wearing their old spectacles, took out a small, folded "Illustrated Seven Beauties Picture" from their pockets to read and sing along. Some took out playing cards and chess pieces to gamble with each other. Some peeled off a piece of old newspaper from their luggage and read it over and over. Some, out of boredom, occasionally met each other's eyes, nodded, and began to talk about ancient and modern times.

They began to talk, but it was all unpleasant narratives: talking about years of famine, talking about the stories of women in small villages who hanged themselves because they ran out of food, talking about the absurd tragedies of strong men being murdered in batches, talking about the increasingly difficult business, talking about this "generation being worse than the last" world...

A middle-aged cloth merchant, with countless lines carved on his sallow face, his eyes dulled by two or three nights of insomnia, could not even maintain the balance of his pronunciation as he reminisced about a scene of life's hardships, his lips trembling like the wings of an autumn cicada.

"These years are truly unlike any I've lived through: even large grains of wheat planted in the fields can't keep people alive, so people have to drift far away from their hometowns, drifting away, not knowing whether they'll live or die; but in the end, they face even greater hardships. Doing business, working, opening workshops, nothing works. People are making too many tricks, and in the end, they're always taking people's lives."

A light of torment flashed in his eyes: "The market is so bad, old fellow, think about it, what way is there to go these days!! I'm already over fifty, and I still don't know if I'll live or die tomorrow. Oh, look, the weather has changed."

His voice, withered and faint like a dying oil lamp, filled the listeners' hearts with dampness, as if they had swallowed a mouthful of cold water. Some people's enthusiasm gradually withered away, and everyone was silent, as if pondering something.

Lightly and sparsely, in the fog, rain began to fall outside, and the wind blowing in through the window cracks was uncomfortably cold. The boatman called out softly from outside: "Esteemed guests, please rest early. The fog will clear tonight and we'll set sail. We'll be there before dawn tomorrow."

Everyone silently went to their bunks, thinking, "If only the fog would clear sooner."

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Margaret Sullavan's "Runaway Marriage" 301

Carefully Planned Secrets Are Difficult to Keep

Leaving the Screen to Be a Full-Time Wife

Margaret Sullavan and her director William Wyler's "runaway marriage" was originally carefully planned and foolproof. But the result was beyond their expectations. They thought that no one would know before the announcement, and they decided that the day of their marriage announcement would be when they finished their new film "The Good Fairy" and went out for their honeymoon hand in hand. This was their plan. Unexpectedly, a small glitch occurred. When their secret was leaked out, Hollywood didn't believe it. That day was Sunday night, and some people sitting next to the radio only heard Wingell announce a very simple piece of news, saying that Margaret Sullavan and her director William Wyler had married this morning at 11 o'clock in Yuma. Even if the newlyweds Margaret and William heard this simple piece of news, they would be surprised and disbelieving, because they believed that their secret was impossible to leak. Besides the new couple, there were two other people involved in the secret, William Wyler's lawyer and one of Margaret Sullavan's close friends, but they would never reveal this secret. So how did the outside world know? This shows that in the United States, where the news industry is developed, it is not easy to keep anything secret. According to their plan, they would slip away hand in hand after finishing work on Saturday night and return to work as usual on Monday, so that no one would know. They filmed on Saturday night until 4 am on Sunday before finishing. At 6 am, Margaret, William, and William's lawyer boarded the pre-rented 15-seater plane and set off for Yuma. Besides the three of them, there was also a pilot and no one else. Setting out at dawn with the dew, the sunrise in the clouds, the celestial couple, proudly roaming the sky, their joy is naturally self-evident. Everything went smoothly in Yuma. The pastor was also arranged in advance. After the new couple kissed after the ceremony, they returned to the airfield hand in hand. When Margaret was about to jump back into the plane, there was another young lady at the airfield waiting for another plane to land. She recognized that the person jumping into the plane and the two men who were leaving in a hurry was a certain Hollywood star. She casually said a word to the airfield staff, and then the news spread! When they were riding the wind and feeling like immortals, the telegraph lines and wireless machines were busy ringing. The romance between Margaret Sullavan and William Wyler was extremely swift and silent, and did not attract anyone's attention beforehand. On the surface, they were very incompatible. Although Margaret admired William Wyler's directing talent very much, in the year and a half they knew each other, she never expected to marry Wyler. They often argued about this and that on the set. Margaret's personality is very strong. She says whatever she thinks with her straightforward temperament. She doesn't like working at night. She gave Wyler a nickname called Owl because he liked working at night. She also complained that Wyler worked too slowly, saying that he would never finish a film. At the same time, she was in close contact with Corinne Murray's ex-husband, John McCormick. She never talked to her director for more than three sentences on the set. She got along very well with the general staff and had a lot of fun. But recently, Margaret often ate lunch at the same table with her director in the dining room. The director would talk incessantly, and Margaret would sit silently and listen. However, people always thought they were talking about things in the film and would never think that love would happen between them. But Margaret's personality suddenly changed. She no longer resisted filming at night and often filmed happily from dusk until dawn. This was something that even she herself found hard to believe. This went on for almost two weeks. Suddenly one day, she discovered that she had fallen in love with her director, deeply in love. The rest is self-explanatory. But Margaret is a person who goes forward without looking back. She wants to have children as soon as she gets married. Therefore, it is expected that she will leave the film industry and become a full-time wife.

Film Review

Review of "Behold My Wife" 302

— Ling He

Behold My Wife丨Cathay

Since "Madame Butterfly", Sylvia Sidney, who has a distinct Eastern woman flavor, has been warmly noticed by Chinese audiences, so her "Behold My Wife" has once again caused a sensation among Shanghai audiences in the New Year. In addition to "Madame Butterfly", she also played very well in "Street Scene". However, she has not had any other successful performances. As for this film, her acting skills are not particularly outstanding, at best, she is only dutiful, because the story does not suit her personality.

In this film, only the process of Manley's suicide is very well written. Regardless of the arrangement of the atmosphere or the handling of the scene, and due to Ann Sheridan's excellent acting skills (although there are not many scenes), that scene is indeed very emotional, becoming the most outstanding and wonderful part of the work. If this film is valuable, then it is only expressed here.

From the time the young master angrily left home, from the door of the house to the door of the car, quickly writing several doors in a row, and then using cars and alcohol to describe his wandering and the psychological perversion of his suicidal body, also shows the director's cleverness. From the beginning until the young master meets Sylvia Sidney in the hotel, "Behold My Wife" tightly grasps the audience's mood and pays attention to future developments. But the fact is not like this, from then on, the progress of the play is very mediocre. The twists and turns of the plot are stiff and artificial, and it can be said that there is simply no drama, but only the narration of the story. Even in the highest conflict, when Sylvia Sidney realizes that the young master's husband does not sincerely love her, but only uses her as a tool to anger his family, (the young master does not want her to take off her Indian costume,) that scene is also so weak, and Sylvia Sidney's performance is also so unfamiliar. All the way until Sylvia Sidney goes to jail for someone else's crime, and the young master's husband conscientiously takes the blame for his wife, it is even more unreasonable to make up a story for the sake of the story. The degree of childishness and absurdity is beyond compare.

In terms of technique, we see that the director's depiction of the personality of the characters in the play is quite commendable in some scenes. For example, writing about the young master's stubborn mother, his father's mediocrity, his sister's treachery, and Sylvia Sidney's Indian's strong and chaste national character, what is expressed is the mother's anxiety, needing alcohol to stimulate, the father's busyness, the sister's cold words and false smiles, and Sylvia Sidney's bold removal of bullets for the young master and her rampage at the train station are all better depictions. But they are not consistently portrayed, and the more the play progresses, the more they lose their original personality. This, like the inability to consistently grasp the atmosphere, shows that the director and playwright do not have the ability to create in depth.

As mentioned above, this is not a successful work. Although it has its individual successes, on the whole, with the problem of being heavy at the beginning and light at the end, the impression it gives people is very fragile.

Review of "Moonlight and Flowers" 303

— Ji Han

Flirtation Walk 丨丨 Great Light Cinema

Judging from Frank Borzage's consistent style, Dick, the soldier in "Moonlight and Flowers," strives for upward mobility, being ashamed of his low status, and seeking advanced studies at a military academy. He eventually rises from a lower-ranking soldier to become a top student in the military academy. This spirit of striving upward has been hinted at in Borzage's earlier works. However, the story of "Moonlight and Flowers" is vulgar.

An officer's daughter falls in love with a lower-ranking soldier, motivating the lower-ranking soldier to strive and climb upward, and then marry the officer's daughter. This vulgar concept almost makes us not believe it is a work by Borzage. In earlier works such as "Seventh Heaven" and "Angel," the characters that appeared were resentful due to poverty, and as a result, they found comfort in love and purity. This style continued until the recent "A Farewell to Arms," which is still a depiction of impoverished life, where the male and female protagonists shed tears of joy amid the cruel living environment for the sake of the purity of love. Of course, the author cannot essentially excavate the sadness of life, and often uses love to dissolve the troubles of life, but the cruel depiction of life's worries makes people cry bitterly. However, "Moonlight and Flowers," as a musical film, does not inherit the previous style. The discovery of purity here is due to the officer's daughter falling in love with the soldier's handsomeness, and then waiting for the lower-ranking soldier to rise in rank before breaking off her engagement with the officer and marrying the soldier. This expression of purity is truly too vulgar. Can we still see a bit of the sadness of life? The so-called concept of love transcending everything shows that Borzage is gradually becoming mediocre.

Taking a step back, the story structure here is also extremely imprecise. For example, Dick's friend is transferred to Shanghai, and other than receiving a few letters from Dick, he does almost nothing. Later, when they meet, it is just a very unimportant scene. This character seems superfluous in the play, and therefore interrupts the development of the main storyline several times. Also, it is very sudden that the officer's daughter's fiancé shakes hands with Dick, allowing his fiancée to marry Dick. There should at least be a scene of the engaged couple breaking up.

However, some scenes are indeed very good. The most important is the so-called Flirtation Walk, with its bright moonlight, crisp singing, charming dance, and gentle flirtation. Due to the excellent photography, appropriate camera angles, composition of the shots, and the atmosphere at the time, everything is very beautiful. In addition, the several military drills are also extremely beautiful. The military music, like the aforementioned scenes, is also fascinating. From these aspects, it still fully illustrates the excellence of Borzage's technique. The expression methods of a famous director are, after all, extraordinary.

Like other recent American films, this is full of vigor, brisk, uplifting, and humorous, forming a lovely tragicomedy. It makes people feel light and harmonious, but because of this, it has lost Borzage's consistent rigorous content, and the calm tone and serious atmosphere are absent here. As a musical film, this is quite original and unique, at least preserving a simple atmosphere, not as strongly imbued with the scent of gold as "The Springtime of Life" and "Gold Diggers of 1935". However, as mentioned above, due to the determination of the content, this work ultimately only belongs to the category of ordinary and vulgar.

The Leisure Life of Foreign Stars 304

— Hua Shu

The most fashionable leisure activities for Chinese stars are dancing, watching plays, eating fancy dishes, and swimming in the summer. But let's see what these foreign stars do in their spare time.

Greta Garbo often wears black glasses and strolls down the street, looking at the merchandise in the shop windows. Sometimes she sneaks into a small café alone, sits in a corner, and drinks a cup of coffee. When someone notices her, she quickly runs away.

Bette Davis often gazes out of the window on high rooftops, or spends very little money to eat something at small snack shops.

Johnny Weissmuller loves to swim. Regardless of the weather, he always spends his life in the pool.

When Shirley Temple visits the park, she only brings a dog, and sits silently among the deep branches, watching others. She can see people, but people cannot see her, even in very cold and snowy weather.

Ann Harding likes to go to the countryside and the fields. Sometimes she lingers in the California countryside, and the company searches for her everywhere because of the filming schedule. In the end, they find her in a remote area.

Robert Montgomery spends half of his free time at home reading newspapers and magazines, and the other half at sports fields, theaters, coffee shops, or restaurants. Sometimes, when he's in a good mood, he goes to five or six restaurants a day, which is also common.

Whenever Marlene Dietrich has free time, she likes to chat and play with a few friends, or ride a bicycle. In the winter, she hopes for snow because she likes to ice skate in the snow.

Editorial Department of the Film Special Publication

Film Novel

David Copperfield (Part 3) 306

— Liu Cun

This shattered his heart, and he couldn't care less about what happened to himself. His heart and his brain were momentarily numb. When Mr. Murdstone told him that he was going to send him to London to be an apprentice in the wine shop opened by Murdstone and Grinby, he could only speak one word at a time, and his language was incoherent. So he soon went to London to be an apprentice in Murdstone and Grinby's wine shop, where he could have a bowl of rice to eat, some pocket money, and a place to sleep.

In the wine shop, he leaned his small back against the huge wooden barrels every day, washing bottles all day long. A group of older children, making fun of his gentlemanly demeanor, mocked him at all times, and there was no joy to speak of. The only joy he got in London was interacting with the family of his landlord, Mr. Micawber. He soon developed a sincere affection for Mr. and Mrs. Micawber. He was also very friendly with their four noisy children and their not very useful servant, Creakle, who was a child taken from the Lowood Orphan Asylum.

Mr. Micawber's family was something he had never expected in his life. Mr. Micawber was also someone he had never seen before. Before seeing him, you had to see one of his long legs first, because he often climbed into the house through the skylight to avoid being seen by the noisy creditors outside the door demanding payment. But as soon as he saw David, he happily met him and extended a thick, fat hand to shake his. He turned his head and looked at Mrs. Micawber, cheerfully telling her that he had "severed ties" with the grocery store because they had cut off the commission he had hoped for.

Mrs. Micawber, hearing this, said mournfully, "But what about my dear Wilkins' future? If I say we still have to talk about it, would you say I'm wrong?" Mr. Micawber then said, "My dear, remember the words 'After the worst, comes the best.' I have thoroughly planned all kinds of businesses. I have chosen the wine-making industry. Simply put, I have written several letters to important winemakers in various places, stating my qualifications and wanting to serve them. All the details have not yet been determined, but I firmly believe that some opportunities will be discovered in this."

Outside the door, a group of creditors clamored for Mr. Micawber to repay his debts, otherwise, they would eat his flesh. Inside the door, a group of children shouted strangely, fighting each other. Creakle took an oil drum and fed them things to eat. But Mr. Micawber was a perpetually optimistic man, looking at his little tenant, David, with a rather content and happy expression. He quietly waited for any opportunity to be discovered. David lived with them for a few months and was also very happy. They made him forget his own sorrowful fate and arduous work. But he was not blessed by heaven, and even Mr. Micawber's family was taken away. One day at noon, Creakle brought him bad news. That night, he found Mr. Micawber's entire family imprisoned for failing to repay their debts.

But if David thought they must be sad and weeping, he was wrong, because when David went to the prison to see them, Mr. and Mrs. Micawber were toasting with a large bowl of grog. Celebrating? That's right, because not long after they were imprisoned, Mrs. Micawber's family bravely came to their rescue, paying off all their debts and promising to find Mr. Micawber two positions at the Customs House of Gravesend. Therefore, Mr. Micawber felt leisurely and happy, and good fortune would soon descend. Mr. Micawber was certainly very happy, but their relocation caused David to lose the few good companions he had in London. After waving his hand and sending them away, his heart was full of sorrow, and he realized the bitterness of his abandonment and isolation, with no relatives to turn to. (To be continued)
